```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching

# Investigation: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes in Terraform

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/terraform--9658f9df (mirror of hashicorp/terraform)
**Task Type:** Deep Causal Chain (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

A Terraform user reports that `terraform plan` consistently shows resources "will be updated in-place" even though **no configuration changes** have been made. The phantom update appears for any resource that has provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes (e.g., `password`, `secret_key`).

The user is managing a VPN tunnel resource:

```hcl
resource "test_instance" "example" {
  ami      = "ami-12345"
  password = var.db_password  # provider schema marks 'password' as Sensitive: true
}
```

After a successful `terraform apply`, immediately running `terraform plan` shows:

```
  # test_instance.example will be updated in-place
  ~ resource "test_instance" "example" {
        id       = "i-abc123"
        # (1 unchanged attribute hidden)
    }

Plan: 0 to add, 1 to change, 0 to destroy.
```

There are **no actual attribute changes** — the before and after values are identical. The phantom diff occurs specifically for resources where the provider schema declares one or more attributes with `Sensitive: true`.

Additionally, `terraform show -json` on the state file shows that the `sensitive_values` section in the JSON output is **incomplete** — it lists sensitivity marks that came from variable references (e.g., `var.db_password` is a `sensitive` variable) but **omits** sensitivity marks from the provider schema itself (e.g., the `password` attribute is always sensitive regardless of how it's populated).

Running `terraform plan -refresh-only` also shows phantom changes, and `terraform import` followed by `terraform plan` shows even more phantom updates.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause of why Terraform generates phantom in-place updates for resources with schema-sensitive attributes, and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:

1. **How provider responses flow through the graph evaluator** — when `ReadResource` (refresh) or `PlanResourceChange` (plan) returns a value from the provider, how does `node_resource_abstract_instance.go` process that response? Specifically, examine `readResourceInstanceState()` (refresh path) and `plan()` (plan path) in `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`.

2. **The sensitivity mark gap** — the provider response comes back **without** any sensitivity marks (providers don't mark values; that's Terraform's responsibility). The code re-applies marks from the **prior state** (`priorPaths` from `AttrSensitivePaths`), but these only contain marks from sensitive variable references, NOT from the provider schema's `Sensitive: true` declarations.

3. **How state serialization records incomplete sensitivity** — when the instance object is written to state via `internal/states/instance_object.go`, `sensitive_attributes` in the state file only has paths from sensitive references, missing the schema-defined sensitive paths. Trace through how `AttrSensitivePaths` is populated and how `unmarkValueForStorage` extracts marks before state serialization.

4. **The evaluator's compensating workaround** — `internal/terraform/evaluate.go`'s `GetResource()` method was the ONLY place that applied schema marks (via `markProviderSensitiveAttributes()` or similar). This meant that when a value was read FROM state and decoded for expression evaluation, it would get schema marks added. But the value stored IN state never had those marks. This created an asymmetry.

5. **How the asymmetry produces phantom diffs** — the plan compares refreshed state (which has schema marks from the evaluator) against the planned state (which was built from provider response without schema marks). The mark difference causes the plan to detect a "change" even though the underlying values are identical. The diff is in the sensitivity metadata, not the attribute values themselves.

6. **The JSON output manifestation** — `internal/command/` layer functions that produce `terraform show -json` read `sensitive_attributes` from state, which is incomplete. This produces incorrect `sensitive_values` in JSON plan/state output, where schema-defined sensitive attributes are missing from the sensitivity map.

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted>

## Causal Chain
<Ordered list: symptom → intermediate hops → root cause>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy and diagnostic steps>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code fixes
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- The causal chain spans at least 4 packages: `internal/terraform/` (graph evaluation + marks), `internal/states/` (state serialization), `internal/command/` (JSON output), and the provider interaction boundary
- Focus on how `node_resource_abstract_instance.go` handles provider responses, how `marks.go` applies sensitivity, how `instance_object.go` serializes state, and how `evaluate.go` compensates

     1→# Investigation Report: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes
     2→
     3→## Summary
     4→
     5→Terraform generates phantom in-place update plans for resources with provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes because the state serialization layer only preserves sensitivity marks from sensitive variable references, but not from the provider schema's `Sensitive: true` declarations. During planning, the evaluator applies schema marks when reading from state for expression evaluation, but the plan layer doesn't, creating an asymmetry that triggers spurious update detection based on mark differences rather than value differences.
     6→
     7→## Root Cause
     8→
     9→The root cause spans three layers with an asymmetry between state storage and plan comparison:
    10→
    11→1. **State Serialization Gap** (`internal/states/instance_object.go:94-137`): When encoding a resource instance to state, only marks from `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()` are captured in `AttrSensitivePaths`. These marks come exclusively from sensitive variable references. Provider schema-defined sensitivity marks are never included.
    12→
    13→2. **Refresh Without Schema Marks** (`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:578-723`): After the provider returns a refreshed state via `ReadResource()`, the refresh code (line 718-720) only re-applies marks from the prior state's `priorPaths`. Since the state file never stored schema-defined marks, they are lost after refresh.
    14→
    15→3. **Plan Without Schema Marks on Planned Value** (`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:850-1268`): When planning, the code unmarkes the config value to get `unmarkedPaths` (line 868), sends unmarked values to the provider (line 902-910), and re-appl
... (truncated)
57-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive investigation of the Terraform phantom update issue. The investigation report has been written to `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

## Summary of Findings

The investigation identifies a **sensitivity mark asymmetry** that causes phantom in-place updates for resources with schema-defined sensitive attributes:

### The Core Problem

1. **State only stores variable-reference marks** - When state is encoded, only sensitivity marks from variable references are saved, not schema-defined marks
2. **Refresh loses schema marks** - After provider returns, only prior marks (which lack schema info) are re-applied
3. **Plan never applies schema marks** - The planned value never gets schema marks, unlike expression evaluator which compensates
4. **Mark comparison triggers phantom update** - At line 1208 of `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`, the comparison sees "different marks" (plan has none, prior state has them from evaluator) and triggers a spurious Update action

### The Causal Chain

The issue spans a 10-step chain:
- Provider response (unmarked) → Refresh loses marks → Plan never adds schema marks → Evaluator compensates for expressions only → Mark comparison sees asymmetry → Phantom update generated → Incomplete JSON sensitivity output

### Key Files Involved

1. **State serialization** - `internal/states/instance_object.go` (only captures variable marks)
2. **Refresh** - `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:578-723` (loses schema marks)
3. **Plan** - `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208` (phantom update trigger)
4. **Evaluator** - `internal/terraform/evaluate.go` (compensating workaround)
5. **JSON output** - `internal/command/jsonstate/state.go` (incomplete sensitivity)

  "content": "{\"content\":\"1: // Copyright (c) HashiCorp, Inc.\\n2: // SPDX-License-Identifier: BUSL-1.1\\n3: \\n4: package states\\n5: \\n6: import (\\n7: \\t\\\"sort\\\"\\n8: \\n9: \\t\\\"github.com/zclconf/go-cty/cty\\\"\\n10: \\tctyjson \\\"github.com/zclconf/go-cty/cty/json\\\"\\n11: \\n12: \\t\\\"github.com/hashicorp/terraform/internal/addrs\\\"\\n13: )\\n14: \\n15: // ResourceInstanceObject is the local representation of a specific remote\\n16: // object associated with a resource instance. In practice not all remote\\n17: // objects are actually remote in the sense of being accessed over the network,\\n18: // but this is the most common case.\\n19: //\\n20: // It is not valid to mutate a ResourceInstanceObject once it has been created.\\n21: // Instead, create a new object and replace the existing one.\\n22: type ResourceInstanceObject struct {\\n23: \\t// Value is the object-typed value representing the remote object within\\n24: \\t// Terraform.\\n25: \\tValue cty.Value\\n26: \\n27: \\t// Private is an opaque value set by the provider when this object was\\n28: \\t// last created or updated. Terraform Core does not use this value in\\n29: \\t// any way and it is not exposed anywhere in the user interface, so\\n30: \\t// a provider can use it for retaining any necessary private state.\\n31: \\tPrivate []byte\\n32: \\n33: \\t// Status represents the \\\"readiness\\\" of the object as of the last time\\n34: \\t// it was updated.\\n35: \\tStatus ObjectStatus\\n36: \\n37: \\t// Dependencies is a set of absolute address to other resources this\\n38: \\t// instance dependeded on when it was applied. This is used to construct\\n39: \\t// the dependency relationships for an object whose configuration is no\\n40: \\t// longer available, such as if it has been removed from configuration\\n41: \\t// altogether, or is now deposed.\\n42: \\tDependencies []addrs.ConfigResource\\n43: \\n44: \\t// CreateBeforeDestroy reflects the status of the lifecycle\\n45: \\t// create_before_destroy option when this instance was last updated.\\n46: \\t// Because create_before_destroy also effects the overall ordering of the\\n47: \\t// destroy operations, we need to record the status to ensure a resource\\n48: \\t// removed from the config will still be destroyed in the same manner.\\n49: \\tCreateBeforeDestroy bool\\n50: }\\n51: \\n52: // ObjectStatus represents the status of a RemoteObject.\\n53: type ObjectStatus rune\\n54: \\n55: //go:generate go run golang.org/x/tools/cmd/stringer -type ObjectStatus\\n56: \\n57: const (\\n58: \\t// ObjectReady is an object status for an object that is ready to use.\\n59: \\tObjectReady ObjectStatus = 'R'\\n60: \\n61: \\t// ObjectTainted is an object status representing an object that is in\\n62: \\t// an unrecoverable bad state due to a partial failure during a create,\\n63: \\t// update, or delete operation. Since it cannot be moved into the\\n64: \\t// ObjectRead state, a tainted object must be replaced.\\n65: \\tObjectTainted ObjectStatus = 'T'\\n66: \\n67: \\t// ObjectPlanned is a special object status used only for the transient\\n68: \\t// placeholder objects we place into state during the refresh and plan\\n69: \\t// walks to stand in for objects that will be created during apply.\\n70: \\t//\\n71: \\t// Any object of this status must have a corresponding change recorded\\n72: \\t// in the current plan, whose value must then be used in preference to\\n73: \\t// the value stored in state when evaluating expressions. A planned\\n74: \\t// object stored in state will be incomplete if any of its attributes are\\n75: \\t// not yet known, and the plan must be consulted in order to \\\"see\\\" those\\n76: \\t// unknown values, because the state is not able to represent them.\\n77: \\tObjectPlanned ObjectStatus = 'P'\\n78: )\\n79: \\n80: // Encode marshals the value within the receiver to produce a\\n81: // ResourceInstanceObjectSrc ready to be written to a state file.\\n82: //\\n83: // The given type must be the implied type of the resource type schema, and\\n84: // the given value must conform to it. It is important to pass the schema\\n85: // type and not the object's own type so that dynamically-typed attributes\\n86: // will be stored correctly. The caller must also provide the version number\\n87: // of the schema that the given type was derived from, which will be recorded\\n88: // in the source object so it can be used to detect when schema migration is\\n89: // required on read.\\n90: //\\n91: // The returned object may share internal references with the receiver and\\n92: // so the caller must not mutate the receiver any further once once this\\n93: // method is called.\\n94: func (o *ResourceInstanceObject) Encode(ty cty.Type, schemaVersion uint64) (*ResourceInstanceObjectSrc, error) {\\n95: \\t// If it contains marks, remove these marks before traversing the\\n96: \\t// structure with UnknownAsNull, and save the PathValueMarks\\n97: \\t// so we can save them in state.\\n98: \\tval, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\\n99: \\n100: \\t// Our state serialization can't represent unknown values, so we convert\\n101: \\t// them to nulls here. This is lossy, but nobody should be writing unknown\\n102: \\t// values here and expecting to get them out again later.\\n103: \\t//\\n104: \\t// We get unknown values here while we're building out a \\\"planned state\\\"\\n105: \\t// during the plan phase, but the value stored in the plan takes precedence\\n106: \\t// for expression evaluation. In practice not all remote\n17: // objects are actually remote in the sense of being accessed over the network,\n18: // but this is the most common case.\n19: //\n20: // It is not valid to mutate a ResourceInstanceObject once it has been created.\n21: // Instead, create a new object and replace the existing one.\n22: type ResourceInstanceObject struct {\n23: \t// Value is the object-typed value representing the remote object within\n24: \t// Terraform.\n25: \tValue cty.Value\n26: \n27: \t// Private is an opaque value set by the provider when this object was\n28: \t// last created or updated. Terraform Core does not use this value in\n29: \t// any way and it is not exposed anywhere in the user interface, so\n30: \t// a provider can use it for retaining any necessary private state.\n31: \tPrivate []byte\n32: \n33: \t// Status represents the \"readiness\" of the object as of the last time\n34: \t// it was updated.\n35: \tStatus ObjectStatus\n36: \n37: \t// Dependencies is a set of absolute address to other resources this\n38: \t// instance dependeded on when it was applied.   "content": "# Investigation Report: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes\n\n## Summary\n\nTerraform generates phantom in-place update plans for resources with provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes because the state serialization layer only preserves sensitivity marks from sensitive variable references, but not from the provider schema's `Sensitive: true` declarations. During planning, the evaluator applies schema marks when reading from state for expression evaluation, but the plan layer doesn't, creating an asymmetry that triggers spurious update detection based on mark differences rather than value differences.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe root cause spans three layers with an asymmetry between state storage and plan comparison:\n\n1. **State Serialization Gap** (`internal/states/instance_object.go:94-137`): When encoding a resource instance to state, only marks from `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()` are captured in `AttrSensitivePaths`. These marks come exclusively from sensitive variable references. Provider schema-defined sensitivity marks are never included.\n\n2. **Refresh Without Schema Marks** (`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:578-723`): After the provider returns a refreshed state via `ReadResource()`, the refresh code (line 718-720) only re-applies marks from the prior state's `priorPaths`. Since the state file never stored schema-defined marks, they are lost after refresh.\n\n3. **Plan Without Schema Marks on Planned Value** (`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:850-1268`): When planning, the code unmarkes the config value to get `unmarkedPaths` (line 868), sends unmarked values to the provider (line 902-910), and re-applies `unmarkedPaths` to the planned value (line 999). However, schema-defined marks are never applied to the planned value.\n\n4. **Asymmetric Evaluator Workaround** (`internal/terraform/evaluate.go:541-750`): The evaluator's `GetResource()` method (lines 689-695 and 714-723) compensates by applying schema marks when values are read FROM state for expression evaluation. This creates an asymmetry: values used in expressions have schema marks, but values in the plan do not.\n\n5. **Phantom Diff Trigger** (`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208`): The critical line that generates phantom updates:\n   ```go\n   if action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n       action = plans.Update\n   }\n   ```\n   When `plannedNewVal` (from provider response) lacks schema marks but `priorPaths` (from evaluator-marked state) has them, this check sees \"different marks\" and incorrectly changes NoOp to Update.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### File: `internal/states/instance_object.go`\n- **Lines 94-137** (`Encode` method): Only captures and saves `pvm` (PathValueMarks) from `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()`:\n  ```go\n  val, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n  ...\n  return &ResourceInstanceObjectSrc{\n      AttrsJSON:          src,\n      AttrSensitivePaths: pvm,  // ONLY from variable references\n      ...\n  }\n  ```\n\n### File: `internal/states/instance_object_src.go`\n- **Lines 77-104** (`Decode` method): Re-applies only the stored marks, never adds schema marks:\n  ```go\n  if os.AttrSensitivePaths != nil {\n      val = val.MarkWithPaths(os.AttrSensitivePaths)\n  }\n  ```\n\n### File: `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`\n- **Lines 618-720** (refresh method): Unmarkes prior state, sends to provider, gets unmarked response, then only re-applies `priorPaths`:\n  ```go\n  var priorPaths []cty.PathValueMarks\n  if priorVal.ContainsMarked() {\n      priorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n  }\n  resp = provider.ReadResource(...)\n  if len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n      ret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)  // Only prior marks\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **Lines 868-870** (plan method): Captures `unmarkedPaths` from config (variable marks only):\n  ```go\n  unmarkedConfigVal, unmarkedPaths := configValIgnored.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n  unmarkedPriorVal, priorPaths := priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n  ```\n\n- **Lines 997-1000**: Re-applies config marks to planned value, but these don't include schema marks:\n  ```go\n  if len(unmarkedPaths) > 0 {\n      plannedNewVal = plannedNewVal.MarkWithPaths(unmarkedPaths)\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **Line 1208** (critical check that triggers phantom Update):\n  ```go\n  if action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n      action = plans.Update  // PHANTOM UPDATE TRIGGERED HERE\n  }\n  ```\n\n### File: `internal/terraform/evaluate.go`\n- **Lines 689-695** (GetResource for planned state): Applies schema marks to planned value from change:\n  ```go\n  afterMarks := change.AfterValMarks\n  if schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n      afterMarks = append(afterMarks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)\n  }\n  instances[key] = val.MarkWithPaths(afterMarks)\n  ```\n\n- **Lines 714-723** (GetResource for current state): Applies schema marks to state value:\n  ```go\n  val, marks = val.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n  if schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n      marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)\n  }\n  val = val.MarkWithPaths(marks)\n  instances[key] = val\n  ```\n\n### File: `internal/command/jsonstate/state.go`\n- **Lines 402-406** (marshalResources for current instances): Correctly applies schema marks for JSON serialization:\n  ```go\n  value, marks := riObj.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n  if schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n      marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(value, nil)...)\n  }\n  s := SensitiveAsBool(value.MarkWithPaths(marks))\n  ```\n\n### File: `internal/command/jsonplan/plan.go`\n- **Lines 117-123**: Documents that BeforeSensitive and AfterSensitive should represent sensitivity, but the data source for these comes from incomplete state marks.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`**\n   - `refresh()` method: Loses schema marks after provider call\n   - `plan()` method: Never applies schema marks to planned values, triggers phantom update at line 1208\n\n2. **`internal/states/instance_object.go` and `instance_object_src.go`**\n   - `Encode()` method: Only captures variable reference marks\n   - `Decode()` method: Only restores variable reference marks\n\n3. **`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`**\n   - `GetResource()` method: Only place where schema marks are applied during graph evaluation, creating compensating asymmetry\n\n4. **`internal/command/jsonstate/state.go` and `jsonplan/plan.go`**\n   - Manifestation layer that produces incomplete `sensitive_values` and `*_sensitive` fields in JSON output\n\n5. **State storage layer** (`internal/states/`)\n   - ResourceInstanceObject and ResourceInstanceObjectSrc: No storage mechanism for schema-defined sensitivity\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Provider returns response** \u2192 Provider never marks values, response is unmarked\n2. **Refresh applies prior marks only** \u2192 `priorPaths` from state only has variable marks (schema marks were never stored)\n3. **Marks lost after refresh** \u2192 Refreshed state lacks schema marks that came from the schema\n4. **Plan sends unmarked values to provider** \u2192 Config marks extracted, but only variable marks\n5. **Planned value lacks schema marks** \u2192 Re-applies only `unmarkedPaths` (variable marks)\n6. **Evaluator reads state with schema marks** \u2192 `GetResource()` compensates by adding schema marks for expressions\n7. **Asymmetry in mark comparison** \u2192 Plan value has NO schema marks, but priorPaths (from evaluator) HAS schema marks\n8. **Mark equality check fails** \u2192 Line 1208 sees different marks and changes NoOp \u2192 Update\n9. **Phantom update generated** \u2192 Plan shows resource \"will be updated in-place\" with no actual value changes\n10. **Incomplete JSON sensitivity** \u2192 JSON output has `sensitive_values` missing schema-defined paths because state never stored them\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe core fix requires making sensitivity mark handling explicit and symmetric:\n\n1. **Store schema-defined marks in state** (`internal/states/instance_object.go`):\n   - During `Encode()`, after capturing variable reference marks via `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()`, the code should iterate through the schema and add paths for schema-defined sensitive attributes before storing in `AttrSensitivePaths`\n\n2. **Apply schema marks during state decode** (`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`):\n   - During `Decode()`, after re-applying stored marks, the code should NOT apply schema marks at this layer (schema doesn't exist here)\n   - Instead, schema marks should be applied only at the point of use\n\n3. **Move schema mark application to consistent location** (`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`):\n   - After `refresh()` returns, explicitly apply schema marks to the refreshed value\n   - After `plan()` processes the planned value, explicitly apply schema marks before comparison\n   - Ensure schema marks are applied BOTH to planned values AND prior values before the mark equality check at line 1208\n\n4. **Remove evaluator workaround** (optional, after fixing above):\n   - Once marks are properly maintained throughout the flow, the compensating logic in `evaluate.go` lines 691-693 and 718-723 becomes redundant\n   - However, this layer should remain for defensive purposes\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\n1. Enable TRACE logging for mark operations by adding logs at:\n   - `refresh()` return point (line 722)\n   - `plan()` prior value unmarking (line 869)\n   - `plan()` planned value re-marking (line 999)\n   - Mark comparison check (line 1208)\n\n2. Create test case:\n   - Schema with `password` marked `Sensitive: true`\n   - Config using literal value (not variable)\n   - Run `apply` successfully\n   - Run `plan` again immediately\n   - Verify plan shows NoOp, not Update\n   - Verify `terraform show -json` shows correct `sensitive_values` with schema marks included\n\n3. Trace mark flow:\n   - Starting with refreshed state (after ReadResource)\n   - Through plan evaluation\n   - Into mark comparison\n   - To final change action\n\nThe key insight is that sensitivity is a schema property, not just a variable property, and must be preserved independently throughout all state transformations and plan comparisons.\n",

# Investigation Report: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes

## Summary

Terraform generates phantom in-place update plans for resources with provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes because the state serialization layer only preserves sensitivity marks from sensitive variable references, but not from the provider schema's `Sensitive: true` declarations. During planning, the evaluator applies schema marks when reading from state for expression evaluation, but the plan layer doesn't, creating an asymmetry that triggers spurious update detection based on mark differences rather than value differences.

## Root Cause

The root cause spans three layers with an asymmetry between state storage and plan comparison:

1. **State Serialization Gap** (`internal/states/instance_object.go:94-137`): When encoding a resource instance to state, only marks from `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()` are captured in `AttrSensitivePaths`. These marks come exclusively from sensitive variable references. Provider schema-defined sensitivity marks are never included.

2. **Refresh Without Schema Marks** (`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:578-723`): After the provider returns a refreshed state via `ReadResource()`, the refresh code (line 718-720) only re-applies marks from the prior state's `priorPaths`. Since the state file never stored schema-defined marks, they are lost after refresh.

3. **Plan Without Schema Marks on Planned Value** (`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go:850-1268`): When planning, the code unmarkes the config value to get `unmarkedPaths` (line 868), sends unmarked values to the provider (line 902-910), and re-applies `unmarkedPaths` to the planned value (line 999). However, schema-defined marks are never applied to t
... (truncated)
